Q: Which sentence between X and Y describes two observations R and S more plausibly?
R: Jane was a professor teaching piano to students.
S: Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book.
X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day.
A: Let's think step by step.Observation R states that Jane is a professor teaching piano to students. Observation S states that Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book. Sentence X describes two observations, one being that Jane has students and the other being that two of them were early for their lessons. Sentence Y describes that none of Jane's students had a lesson that day. 

Since observation R states that Jane is a professor teaching piano to students, it is more plausible that sentence X describes two observations more accurately. Sentence Y contradicts observation R, making it less plausible. Therefore, the sentence "Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons" in sentence X describes two observations R and S more plausibly. 
Therefore, the answer is X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.

Therefore, the answer is Y: Jason's friend made his parents upset.
